<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-72] [configuration] Escaping comma in xml tag attributes does not work</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-72</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;First of all, I know that is as already been discuted, but calling&lt;br/&gt;
config.getString(key) really should not tokenize value and return the first string.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;But I know the implication of this modification to jakarta projects using this&lt;br/&gt;
method, so I will stop here.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;With a configuration like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;tag attribute1=&quot;a,b,c&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
     attribute2=&quot;a\,b\,c&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
 &amp;lt;element1&amp;gt;a,b,c&amp;lt;/element1&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
 &amp;lt;element2&amp;gt;a\,b\,c&amp;lt;element2&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/tag&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I would expect :&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;config.getString(&quot;attribute1&quot;) = &quot;a&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
config.getString(&quot;attribute2&quot;) = &quot;a,b,c&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
config.getString(&quot;element1&quot;) = &quot;a&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
config.getString(&quot;element2&quot;) = &quot;a,b,c&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;But I have&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;config.getString(&quot;attribute1&quot;) = &quot;a&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
config.getString(&quot;attribute2&quot;) = &quot;a&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
config.getString(&quot;element1&quot;) = &quot;a&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
config.getString(&quot;element2&quot;) = &quot;a,b,c&quot;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Escaping the comma does not work into tag attributes&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;I think the problem is within XMLConfiguration#processAttributes(Node,Element),&lt;br/&gt;
nothing here checks is the comma is escaped&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

                            <comment id="12409936" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Sat, 30 Jul 2005 01:36:40 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I did some testing (similar to your test configuration and based on the same&lt;br/&gt;
expectations), but I get completely different results. What I found out is that&lt;br/&gt;
attributes are handled correctly, but elements are not!&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;processAttributes() uses PropertyConverter.split() for splitting the attribute&apos;s&lt;br/&gt;
value(s).This method correctly handles the backslash as escaping character. So&lt;br/&gt;
my test case runs successfully for attributes.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;When processing elements all text nodes occurring in the body of an element are&lt;br/&gt;
just accumulated and at the end set to the element&apos;s value. Here no split&lt;br/&gt;
operation is performed, so I always get the comma delimited list when I call&lt;br/&gt;
getString(). This is wrong and I will change this.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Please let me know if this is your problem or if I fully missunderstand you. We&lt;br/&gt;
are talking about the version currently in SVN, do we?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409937" author="fabien.nisol@videotron.ca" created="Sat, 30 Jul 2005 07:40:26 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Hi,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I&apos;m talking about commons-configuration-1.1.jar which I downloaded one month&lt;br/&gt;
ago, and I had to patch my xml configuration to use elements instead of&lt;br/&gt;
attributes. So Yes, in my version the problem is the oposite of yours.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I will re-download svn version ensuring which version it is, and then give you&lt;br/&gt;
some more hint (like a full example with the jar I use). &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I will also check the code to see if my version has the&lt;br/&gt;
PropertyConverter.split() somewhere in the call sequence just to be sure.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I will do this in about two weeks, I&apos;m going on holidays tomorrow, and NO I&apos;m&lt;br/&gt;
not g33k enough to take my portable with me ;D&lt;/p&gt;


</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-71] [configuration] Fake &quot;resources&quot; dependency kills Maven2</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-71</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;This dependency:&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;!-- Fake dependency to test loading configuration files from a JAR --&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;dependency&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
      &amp;lt;id&amp;gt;resources&amp;lt;/id&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
      &amp;lt;version&amp;gt;1.0&amp;lt;/version&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
      &amp;lt;scope&amp;gt;test&amp;lt;/scope&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;/dependency&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;kills Maven 2 because of the transitive nature of Maven2.  Maven2 if it has a dependency on a project &lt;br/&gt;
gets all its dependencies as well.  So resources of course doesn&apos;t exist and fails.   Now, currently the &lt;br/&gt;
Maven2 POM is created FROM the maven1 POM.  &lt;br/&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.ibiblio.org/maven2/commons-configuration/commons-configuration/1.1/commons-&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://www.ibiblio.org/maven2/commons-configuration/commons-configuration/1.1/commons-&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
configuration-1.1.pom&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;We need to either add a Maven2 pom, or just create a fake resources.jar, but in the commons-&lt;br/&gt;
configuration groupId.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342644">CONFIGURATION-71</key>
            <summary>[configuration] Fake &quot;resources&quot; dependency kills Maven2</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>

                            <comment id="12410675" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Thu, 20 Oct 2005 03:56:03 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=16758)&lt;br/&gt;
Patch for project.xml and maven.xml&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This patch removes the resource.jar from the dependencies section in&lt;br/&gt;
project.xml and tweaks maven.xml to explicitely add it to the class path before&lt;br/&gt;
the tests are run.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I am no maven expert, so not sure if this helps to solve the problem. But the&lt;br/&gt;
dependency that causes trouble will be gone.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410676" author="dep4b" created="Thu, 20 Oct 2005 22:38:20 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I think that would do it...   Is there a more &quot;java&quot; way to do it though, the only other niggle is that the test &lt;br/&gt;
would now fail under Maven2 because there wouldn&apos;t be a maven.xml to do this magic....&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It does seem like our test should not require Maven to do magic.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410677" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Fri, 21 Oct 2005 04:26:45 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I think I understand what you mean. However I cannot think about a more &quot;java&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
solution ATM.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This special test case tests whether a configuration file can be loaded from a&lt;br/&gt;
jar. So one would assume that the affected jar must somehow belong to the&lt;br/&gt;
classpath. Maybe it would be possible to do some black magic with custom&lt;br/&gt;
ClassLoaders? But I would rather avoid such a solution (if it works at all).&lt;br/&gt;
Anyone with better ideas?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If this proposed patch was applied, this would save projects that use Maven2 as&lt;br/&gt;
build tool and specify a dependency to commons-configuration, correct? Well,&lt;br/&gt;
then this would be a first step. For the long run we can think about providing a&lt;br/&gt;
pom for Maven2 (which means that I would have to do some research &lt;img class=&quot;emoticon&quot; src=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/emoticons/wink.png&quot; height=&quot;16&quot; width=&quot;16&quot; align=&quot;absmiddle&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410678" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Wed, 2 Nov 2005 22:41:26 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Here is another, more radical approach.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I checked again the test cases that make use of this resources.jar and came to&lt;br/&gt;
the following result: From configuration&apos;s point of view it does not matter&lt;br/&gt;
whether a configuration file is loaded from a jar or elsewhere from the class&lt;br/&gt;
path. In both cases it is simply dealt with a URL (which of course looks&lt;br/&gt;
different). So what we test here is not in the first line our implementation,&lt;br/&gt;
but the Java runtime&apos;s ability to handle different types of URLs transparently.&lt;br/&gt;
The affected test cases do not contribute to the code coverage of our test suite.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So IMHO we could simply remove these tests, thus getting rid of the faked&lt;br/&gt;
dependency at all. Other opinions?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410679" author="dep4b" created="Wed, 2 Nov 2005 23:05:06 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;+1..   I do feel like our unit tests should NOT get in the way of our delivering code, but instead support &lt;br/&gt;
it...  You are right that the test really is not testing Configuration, but testing Java.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410680" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Thu, 3 Nov 2005 05:09:11 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Okay, then I will update the tests correspondingly.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410681" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Fri, 4 Nov 2005 05:55:20 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I removed the fake dependency and updated the tests. I also verified that this&lt;br/&gt;
does not have any impact on our test coverage (using clover). So this can be&lt;br/&gt;
closed now!&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-70] [configuration] XMLConfiguration contructor not loading the resource</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-70</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Problem:&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration(URL url) constructor does not load the the resource specified&lt;br/&gt;
in argument. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Solution:&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration(URL url) constructor must call load(url) method instead of&lt;br/&gt;
load() method.&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;Description:&lt;br/&gt;
In an web application,&lt;br/&gt;
If the resource mentioned is in somex.jar file and the ConfigurationManager&lt;br/&gt;
which loads the resource is in another.jar file. Then using XMLConfiguration(URL&lt;br/&gt;
url) constructor, it gives exception &apos;ConfigurationException&apos;. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;But if we do as follows.&lt;br/&gt;
(new XMLConfiguration()).load(url), then it loads the resource properly.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342830">CONFIGURATION-70</key>
            <summary>[configuration] XMLConfiguration contructor not loading the resource</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>

                            <comment id="12411191" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Fri, 6 Jan 2006 03:18:00 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;In theory, load(URL) should be called by load() if the URL has been correctly&lt;br/&gt;
set. I think, it is possible that load() is called before initialization is&lt;br/&gt;
complete. Can you provide a stack trace of the exception thrown by the&lt;br/&gt;
constructor? Maybe this helps us to understand what happens here.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Thanks.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12411192" author="abhaykale@rediffmail.com" created="Mon, 9 Jan 2006 14:05:03 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;(In reply to comment #1)&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; In theory, load(URL) should be called by load() if the URL has been correctly&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; set. I think, it is possible that load() is called before initialization is&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; complete. Can you provide a stack trace of the exception thrown by the&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; constructor? Maybe this helps us to understand what happens here.&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; &lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; Thanks.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Exception detailed message is :&lt;br/&gt;
org.apache.commons.configuration.ConfigurationException: Cannot locate&lt;br/&gt;
configuration source ExceptionHandler.xml&lt;br/&gt;
CAUSE is null&lt;br/&gt;
STACKTRACE is null &lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12411193" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Tue, 17 Jan 2006 05:40:56 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;(In reply to comment #2)&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; &lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; Exception detailed message is :&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; org.apache.commons.configuration.ConfigurationException: Cannot locate&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; configuration source ExceptionHandler.xml&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; CAUSE is null&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; STACKTRACE is null &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Are you sure the stack trace is null? This is not very useful &lt;img class=&quot;emoticon&quot; src=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/emoticons/sad.png&quot; height=&quot;16&quot; width=&quot;16&quot; align=&quot;absmiddle&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Okay, I stepped through the code, but could not find anything, which seems&lt;br/&gt;
obviously wrong. The only location where the exception you receive is thrown is&lt;br/&gt;
in AbstractFileConfiguration.load(String). This method should not be called at&lt;br/&gt;
all when the constructor that takes an URL is used!&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Are you able to load configuration files from URLs that point to the file system&lt;br/&gt;
or to the same jar file (i.e. does the URL-constructor work for easy cases)? In&lt;br/&gt;
our unit tests such cases do work.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Last, but not least: Do you really use the newest version of configuration&lt;br/&gt;
(1.2)? In 1.1 there were some bugs related to file based configurations.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

&lt;p&gt;PropertiesConfiguration config = new PropertiesConfiguration(&quot;usergui.properties&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-68] [configuration] ConfigurationFactory not working as expected with include path resolution</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-68</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Documentation states that ConfigurationFactory searches includes in a directory&lt;br/&gt;
relative to the one including conf is located...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Actually, some problem in various initializer methods of ConfigurationFactory&lt;br/&gt;
makes it happen a way that is not natural.&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;ConfigurationFactory() empty constructor sets the basePath to &quot;.&quot;. This is okay,&lt;br/&gt;
but when calling setConfigurationFileName, &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;public void setConfigurationFileName(String configurationFileName)&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        File file = new File(configurationFileName).getAbsoluteFile();
        this.configurationFileName = file.getName();
        implicitBasePath = file.getParent();
    }


&lt;p&gt;basePath is not reset to null... so a call to getBasePath will not return the&lt;br/&gt;
implicitBasePath as stated.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public String getBasePath()&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        String path = StringUtils.isEmpty(basePath) ? implicitBasePath : basePath;
        return StringUtils.isEmpty(path) ? &quot;.&quot; : path;
    }


&lt;p&gt;using ConfigurationFactory(String configurationFileName) does not help, since it&lt;br/&gt;
does not use setConfigurationFileName , so it does not set implicitBasePath&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public ConfigurationFactory(String configurationFileName)&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        this.configurationFileName = configurationFileName;
    }

&lt;p&gt;A work-around solution to these problems is to set the basePath to null&lt;br/&gt;
explicitely after instanciation/setup...&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;a possible correction is to modify the constructor and the setter like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public ConfigurationFactory(String configurationFileName)&lt;/p&gt;
    {  
        setConfigurationFileName(configurationFileName);
    }

&lt;p&gt;    public void setConfigurationFileName(String configurationFileName)&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        File file = new File(configurationFileName).getAbsoluteFile();
        this.configurationFileName = file.getName();
        this.basePath = null;
        implicitBasePath = file.getParent();
    }</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342299">CONFIGURATION-68</key>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-67] [configuration] HierarchicalXMLConfiguration: Phantom-Keys with ...[@xml:base] when using nested XML-Files</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-67</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Hello,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I just tried the build from the newest nightly source code an get a strange&lt;br/&gt;
behaviour for HierarchicalXMLConfiguration in&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://cvs.apache.org/builds/jakarta-commons/nightly/commons-configuration/commons-configuration-src-20041222.zip&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://cvs.apache.org/builds/jakarta-commons/nightly/commons-configuration/commons-configuration-src-20041222.zip&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
if I use nested XML-Configuration-Files.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I tried the following:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul class=&quot;alternate&quot; type=&quot;square&quot;&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;I have a XML-Configuration file super.xml. Within this file, I define an&lt;br/&gt;
!ENTITY pointing to another XML-File sub.xml.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;This entity is used within the original XML-File super.xml to include the&lt;br/&gt;
other XML-File sub.xml.&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;I load the configuration from the original XML-File super.xml.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;When I now print all keys contained in the HierarchicalXMLConfiguration, I get&lt;br/&gt;
for every element from sub.xml an extra configuration entry with the element&lt;br/&gt;
followed by &lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;@xml:base&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt; as the key and the complete URL to sub.xml as the value.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;As an example, consider the following code:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        try {&lt;br/&gt;
            FileConfiguration myHierarchicalXMLConfig = new&lt;br/&gt;
HierarchicalXMLConfiguration();&lt;br/&gt;
            FileConfiguration myXMLConfig = new XMLConfiguration();&lt;br/&gt;
            Iterator iter;&lt;br/&gt;
            String currentKey;&lt;br/&gt;
            myHierarchicalXMLConfig.load(&quot;super.xml&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
            iter = myHierarchicalXMLConfig.getKeys(&quot;INT&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
            while (iter.hasNext()) &lt;/p&gt;
{
                currentKey = (String) iter.next();
                System.out.println(&quot;HierarchicalXMLConfiguration: &quot;
                        + currentKey + &quot; &quot;
                        + myHierarchicalXMLConfig.getProperty(currentKey));
            }
&lt;p&gt;            myXMLConfig.load(&quot;vFConfig.xml&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
            iter = myXMLConfig.getKeys(&quot;INT&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
            while (iter.hasNext()) &lt;/p&gt;
{
                currentKey = (String) iter.next();
                System.out.println(&quot;XMLConfiguration: &quot; + currentKey + &quot; &quot;
                        + myXMLConfig.getProperty(currentKey));
            }
&lt;p&gt;        } catch (ConfigurationException e) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            System.out.println(&quot;ERROR: &quot; + e.toString());
        }

&lt;p&gt;Its output looks like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;HierarchicalXMLConfiguration: INT.SECOND.INT 2&lt;br/&gt;
HierarchicalXMLConfiguration: INT.&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;@xml:base&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;file:///E:/eclipse/workspace/sub.xml&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;file:///E:/eclipse/workspace/sub.xml&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
HierarchicalXMLConfiguration: INT.FIRST.INT 1&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration: INT.FIRST.INT 1&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration: INT.SECOND.INT 2&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;What I expected is that the key INT.&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;@xml:base&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt; should never appear in this&lt;br/&gt;
output as it does for XML-Configuration.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Using the offical 1.0 release of commons-configuration, I get the correct output:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;HierarchicalXMLConfiguration: INT.FIRST.INT 1&lt;br/&gt;
HierarchicalXMLConfiguration: INT.SECOND.INT 2&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration: INT.FIRST.INT 1&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration: INT.SECOND.INT 2&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This output is expected to accour also when using the current nightly source code.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The important part of my included xml-configuratzion-file (&quot;sub.xml&quot;) looks like&lt;br/&gt;
tbis:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;INT&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;FIRST&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;INT&amp;gt;1&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/INT&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/FIRST&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;SECOND&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;INT&amp;gt;2&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/INT&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/SECOND&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/INT&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It would be nice, if this could be fixed again.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Thanks a lot.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Best regards,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Christian Kemmer&lt;/p&gt;</description>

                            <comment id="12408382" author="christian.kemmer@viadee.de" created="Thu, 23 Dec 2004 00:38:56 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=13826)&lt;br/&gt;
included XML-Config-File&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12408383" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Thu, 23 Dec 2004 04:58:50 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Christian,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I digged a bit in the code and here is what I found out:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;First I assume that you use Xerces as XML parser. With Crimson (the JDK&apos;s&lt;br/&gt;
default parser) you cannot read this XML file at all; an exception is thrown&lt;br/&gt;
stating that the relative URI sub.xml cannot be resolved without a base URI.&lt;br/&gt;
This is because we pass a Reader to the parser rather than a file name or a URL.&lt;br/&gt;
Maybe we will have to change this in future (or provide an EntityHandler or&lt;br/&gt;
something).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;But back to your problem: It occurs that Xerces returns an additional attribute&lt;br/&gt;
&quot;xml:base&quot; for each element of the included XML document. The value of this&lt;br/&gt;
attribute is set to the full URL from which this document was loaded. For the&lt;br/&gt;
Configuration class it is impossible to distinguish this attribute from any&lt;br/&gt;
normal attribute. So it is saved as a property in the Configuration. This indeed&lt;br/&gt;
happens for both HierarchicalXMLConfiguration and XMLConfiguration.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;These additional attributes are responsible for the &quot;phantom keys&quot; you face. The&lt;br/&gt;
reason why the keys are returned by HierarchicalXMLConfiguration and not by&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration seems to be a bug in the getKeys(String prefix) method of&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration: this method returns only keys starting with the passed in&lt;br/&gt;
prefix plus a dot, thus missing attributes of the selected element.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So it boils down to that from a Configuration&apos;s point of view your phantom keys&lt;br/&gt;
are valid properties because they are reported by the XML parser. Because of&lt;br/&gt;
that they should be returned by the getKeys() methods.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;My XML knowledge is probably a bit incomplete in this area, does anybody know&lt;br/&gt;
more about these xml:base attributes created by Xerces? Under which conditions&lt;br/&gt;
are they created and what more attributes of this type could occur?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;FYI, I am working on a merge of the two XML configuration classes. Soon there&lt;br/&gt;
will be only one class XMLConfiguration with all the features of (the old)&lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration and HierarchicalXMLConfiguration.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Oliver&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12408384" author="christian.kemmer@viadee.de" created="Fri, 24 Dec 2004 02:21:43 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Hi Oliver,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;thanks for your information.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Yes, I can confirm that the example uses Xalan 2.6.0 with the xerxes parser. I &lt;br/&gt;
also have little knowledge of parsing XML, so I cannot help a lot.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I understand that from a configurations point of view, the new behaviour of &lt;br/&gt;
HierarchicalXMLConfiguration is correct in the nightly builds now. &lt;br/&gt;
Nevertheless, it differs from the current release 1.0, which does not contain &lt;br/&gt;
those xml:base-Keys in the result of getKeys().&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;As the new behaviour of HierarchicalXMLConfiguration is to be considered &lt;br/&gt;
correct and will be included in the next release, I just do the following in &lt;br/&gt;
my code now: Read in the XML-file, iterate over all keys and insert all keys &lt;br/&gt;
but the xml:base-keys in a new object of typ HierarchicalXMLConfiguration. &lt;br/&gt;
That works fine for me and serves as a good workaround.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Perhaps, as a future enhancement, HierarchicalXMLConfiguration could contain a &lt;br/&gt;
removeKeys(Iterator keysToBeRemoved)-method that can be used to remove those &lt;br/&gt;
unwanted keys directly from the configuration. A call could be like this:&lt;br/&gt;
myConfig.removeKeys(myConfig.getKeys(&quot;&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;@xml:base&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&quot;));&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;But for the moment, I have a usefull workaround, so I probably just don&apos;t care &lt;br/&gt;
about this during the next weeks.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Best regards,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Christian Kemmer&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12408385" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Mon, 3 Jan 2005 23:31:50 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Some more information about xml:base attributes can be found e.g. here:&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://xml.apache.org/xerces2-j/faq-xinclude.html&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://xml.apache.org/xerces2-j/faq-xinclude.html&lt;/a&gt; or here:&lt;br/&gt;
www.w3.org/TR/xmlbase/&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;They are obviously important parts of specifications like XLink or XInclude,&lt;br/&gt;
which indicates that they indeed should be treated as normal attributes and kept&lt;br/&gt;
in the set of configuration properties.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;As another workaround to your problem: Would it be possible to avoid the direct&lt;br/&gt;
include in your XML document and instead use a ConfigurationFactory that reads&lt;br/&gt;
the two XML documents from its definition file? If you place these files inside&lt;br/&gt;
an &amp;lt;additional&amp;gt; section, a HierarchicalConfiguration will be constructed with&lt;br/&gt;
the union of both documents.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If this doesn&apos;t help, there is an enhancement request to provide a filter&lt;br/&gt;
decorator (Issue 31281). This should be a solution because it would allow to&lt;br/&gt;
transparently filter out the undesired attributes.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Anyway, I am marking this bug as Wontfix because there is nothing we can do&lt;br/&gt;
about these attributes directly.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-66</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;The getStringArray implementation in CompositeConfiguration doesn&apos;t interpolate&lt;br/&gt;
the tokens like ${foo}, it converts directly the result of getList into an array&lt;br/&gt;
without calling the interpolate method. It would work if getList returns a list&lt;br/&gt;
of interpolated strings, but this is not clearly specified.&lt;/p&gt;</description>

            <title>[CONFIGURATION-65] [configuration] XMLConfiguration cannot load from a jar</title>

Test case to demonstrate the reported bug&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407270" author="jromanda@infophase.com" created="Sat, 21 Aug 2004 02:37:48 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Good point about closing the InputStream. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The previously attached jar file contains the src, class, and config files to &lt;br/&gt;
reproduce the problem (requires commons configuration and supporting jars).  If &lt;br/&gt;
you run the test from the jar file, the ConfigurationFactory will fail caused &lt;br/&gt;
by an underlying FileNotFoundException.  The entire stack trace is below.  If &lt;br/&gt;
you extract the files from the jar and run the test the ConfigurationFactory &lt;br/&gt;
loads ok.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I looking into this a little more and tried loading the XMLConfiguration &lt;br/&gt;
directly which fails either way and is also demonstrated in the test.  The &lt;br/&gt;
XMLConfiguration fails in the constructor using an InputStream with a &lt;br/&gt;
NullPointerException.  Most likely this is because the XMLConfiguration tries &lt;br/&gt;
to treat the InputStream as a File.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The XMLConfiguration class should probably treat source config files as &lt;br/&gt;
InputStreams like the PropertiesConfiguration class does rather than try to &lt;br/&gt;
convert all InputStreams back to Files like it currently does.  My patch &lt;br/&gt;
doesn&apos;t completely resolve the issue, it simply demonstrated the fix for my &lt;br/&gt;
issue.  &lt;/p&gt;

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-64] [configuration] clearXmlProperty doesn&apos;t remove list properties completely</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-64</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;clearXmlProperty in XMLConfiguration stops on the first element found and&lt;br/&gt;
doesn&apos;t examine the whole tree, that means calling clearXmlProperty on a list&lt;br/&gt;
property only remove the first element. For example, given the following&lt;br/&gt;
configuration file:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;key&amp;gt;value1&amp;lt;/key&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;key&amp;gt;value2&amp;lt;/key&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;calling conf.clearProperty(&quot;key&quot;) and saving the configuration will generate the&lt;br/&gt;
following file instead of an empty configuration:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;key&amp;gt;value2&amp;lt;/key&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341586">CONFIGURATION-64</key>
            <summary>[configuration] clearXmlProperty doesn&apos;t remove list properties completely</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>

                            <comment id="12407044" author="brentworden" created="Wed, 21 Jul 2004 22:51:47 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;For the configuration:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;item name=&quot;one&quot;&amp;gt;one&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;two&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;/list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;item name=&quot;three&quot;&amp;gt;three&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;four&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;sublist&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;

  &amp;lt;/list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The patch results in the following behavior changes:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;for conf.clearProperty(&quot;list&quot;) the resulting configuration is:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;for conf.clearProperty(&quot;list.item&quot;) the resulting configuration is:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;/list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;sublist&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
      &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;five&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
      &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;six&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;/sublist&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;/list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;for conf.clearProperty(&quot;list.item&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;@name&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&quot;) the resulting configuration is:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;one&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;two&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;/list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;three&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;four&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;sublist&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
      &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;five&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
      &amp;lt;item&amp;gt;six&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;/sublist&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;/list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407045" author="ebourg" created="Wed, 21 Jul 2004 22:54:13 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Thank you Brent, I&apos;m already working on a patch with a recursive implementation&lt;br/&gt;
of clearXmlProperty but your test case is interesting. Given the following&lt;br/&gt;
configuration:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
        &amp;lt;item name=&quot;foo&quot;&amp;gt;bar&amp;lt;/item&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;/list&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;calling clearProperty(&quot;list&quot;) should not remove the &quot;list.item&quot; property, and&lt;br/&gt;
calling clearProperty(&quot;list.item&quot;) should not remove the &quot;list.item&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;@name&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
property.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-63] [configuration] ConfigurationUtils.locate throws NullPointerException if the context ClassLoader is null</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-63</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Hello,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;When the locate method attempts to find resource location from the context classpath &lt;br/&gt;
(lines 375-384 in ConfigurationUtils.java) it fails (on line 378) if the context &lt;br/&gt;
ClassLoader cannot be retrieved for the current thread.&lt;br/&gt;
I suppose this bug is quite difficult to reproduce. I came accross it when I and a &lt;br/&gt;
colleague of mine were testing a Java API (kept in one jar) that is called from C++ &lt;br/&gt;
application. In the static initializer of a Java class I used the next line to load &lt;br/&gt;
settings:&lt;br/&gt;
config = new PropertiesConfiguration(ConfigurationUtils.locate(&quot;properties/routing.&lt;br/&gt;
properties&quot;));&lt;br/&gt;
It worked fine if the class was used from another Java class that was normally loaded &lt;br/&gt;
by JVM (for example my tests passed). But when my Java classes were executed by JVM &lt;br/&gt;
started from C++ application it resulted in the next exception:&lt;br/&gt;
java.lang.NullPointerException&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.commons.configuration.ConfigurationUtils.&lt;br/&gt;
locate(ConfigurationUtils.java:378)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.commons.configuration.ConfigurationUtils.&lt;br/&gt;
locate(ConfigurationUtils.java:255)&lt;br/&gt;
...&lt;br/&gt;
It is obvious from the ConfigurationUtils code that loader variable got null value &lt;br/&gt;
(line 377) for some reason so the next step threw the exception.&lt;br/&gt;
I suppose this bug can be easily fixed (just to add an additional check if loader is &lt;br/&gt;
not null).&lt;br/&gt;
As a workaround I will try to call locate method with a given base parameter (but it &lt;br/&gt;
needs to determine location of my jar so it is a kind of overheads though it would &lt;br/&gt;
work I hope).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Sorry for my English.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Hope it is useful,&lt;br/&gt;
Denis&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: Windows XP&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: PC&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

Thread.currentThread().setContextClassLoader(RequestManager.class.getClassLoader());&lt;br/&gt;
just before&lt;br/&gt;
config = new PropertiesConfiguration(ConfigurationUtils.locate(&quot;properties/routing.&lt;br/&gt;
properties&quot;));&lt;br/&gt;
And now it works all right.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Thank you very much.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-61] [configuration] JNDIConfiguration and union configuration</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-61</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;JNDIConfiguration seems not to work with ConfigurationFactory when used in the&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;additional&amp;gt; section. The union configuration feature of ConfigurationFactory is&lt;br/&gt;
implemented by calling getKeys() on a Configuration object, iterating through&lt;br/&gt;
the keys, and calling getProperty() for each.&lt;br/&gt;
JNDIConfiguration.getKeys() obviously always returns an empty iterator in my&lt;br/&gt;
tests though the Configuration object is not empty (getString() returns values&lt;br/&gt;
for some keys). I am not sure whether this is a bug in JNDIConfiguration or a&lt;br/&gt;
shortcomming of the JNDI implementation used for testing.&lt;br/&gt;
Another point is that JNDIConfiguration.getProperty() always throws a not&lt;br/&gt;
supported error. This would also blow ConfigurationFactory if getKeys() returned&lt;br/&gt;
a valid iterator. I don&apos;t understand why this error is thrown. In my opinion&lt;br/&gt;
this is a violation of the contract defined by the Configuration interface (the&lt;br/&gt;
same is true for some other methods).&lt;br/&gt;
Attached is an extension to the unit test of ConfigurationFactory that&lt;br/&gt;
demonstrates the problem.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341230">CONFIGURATION-61</key>
            <summary>[configuration] JNDIConfiguration and union configuration</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="oheger">Oliver Heger</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Fri, 30 Jan 2004 03:59:28 +0000</created>
                <updated>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:40 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:40 +0000</resolved>

                            <comment id="12405886" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Fri, 30 Jan 2004 04:00:30 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=10154)&lt;br/&gt;
Another test method for ConfigurationFactory that shows the problem&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12405887" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Fri, 30 Jan 2004 04:42:33 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=10155)&lt;br/&gt;
Test configuration file, copy in conf directory&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12405888" author="dep4b" created="Sun, 15 Feb 2004 19:20:52 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Oliver,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I fixed the immediate bug that makes this fail.  However, I have another &lt;br/&gt;
question.  When loading the configuration from the Configuration Factory, it &lt;br/&gt;
seems like the underlying configs are NOT preserved, but instead a new &lt;br/&gt;
CompositeConfig is made from their values:&lt;br/&gt;
 CompositeConfiguration cc = (CompositeConfiguration)config;&lt;br/&gt;
        // Currently fails, should be 4?  Only 2?&lt;br/&gt;
        //assertEquals(4,cc.getNumberOfConfigurations());&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This I think could be a problem because if I add a config that doesn&apos;t load &lt;br/&gt;
all the values at startup time, but instead at runtime, then it will miss &lt;br/&gt;
values.  I think that is why the JNDIConfiguration value never makes it in:&lt;br/&gt;
    // Fails, because we don&apos;t seem to reach the underlying &lt;br/&gt;
JNDIConfiguraiton        &lt;br/&gt;
        //assertNotNull(config.getProperty(&quot;test.boolean&quot;));&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Becasue there is no JNDIConfiguration object left..&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Maybe this is okay, but we need to define explicitly in the docs that &lt;br/&gt;
configuration values are looked up and stored at startup time, not at runtime..&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I have committed the files, so the unit tests (except the commented out ones) &lt;br/&gt;
pass.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Eric&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12405889" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Mon, 16 Feb 2004 01:41:35 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Eric,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;you are right, the original configs are not saved. Instead on each config the&lt;br/&gt;
getKeys() method is called, and then all keys and their values are stored in a&lt;br/&gt;
new Configuration object.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This is probably the cause why properties obtained from a JNDIConfiguration&lt;br/&gt;
cannot be retrieved. But again, why does the getKeys() method of&lt;br/&gt;
JNDIConfiguration does not return a valid Iterator? Though if all values are&lt;br/&gt;
loaded at runtime, the Configuration interface requires a getKeys() method. So&lt;br/&gt;
it should be safe that the implementation in ConfigurationFactory relies on this.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;What do you think?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Oliver&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                    </comments>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-59] [configuration] XMLConfiguration doesn&apos;t support attribute names with a dot</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-59</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;This appeared to be fixed in 1.0 (&lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-116&quot; title=&quot;[configuration] XMLConfiguration doesn&amp;#39;t support attribute names with a dot&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;CONFIGURATION-116&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;COM-1431&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;) but reappears in 1.1&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;With the new XMLConfiguration, which is hierarchical, properties with a dot in&lt;br/&gt;
their name apparently can be loaded, but the get methods don&apos;t find them.&lt;br/&gt;
For example:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;config&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;test&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
        &amp;lt;myservice-1.0&amp;gt;URL to my service 1.0&amp;lt;/myservice-1.0&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
        &amp;lt;myservice-1.1&amp;gt;URL to my service 1.1&amp;lt;/myservice-1.1&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;/test&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/config&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
I modified my configuration files to split dotted properties, for example:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;some.property&amp;gt;some value&amp;lt;/some.property&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
to&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;some&amp;gt;&amp;lt;property&amp;gt;some value&amp;lt;/property&amp;gt;&amp;lt;/some&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
This way we don&apos;t have to change our code and calls to&lt;br/&gt;
getString(&quot;some.property&quot;) continue to work.&lt;br/&gt;
The problem is that for some properties like myservice-1.0, splitting would&lt;br/&gt;
produce invalid xml:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;myservice-1&amp;gt;&amp;lt;0&amp;gt;URL to my service 1.0&amp;lt;/0&amp;gt;&amp;lt;/myservice-1&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
so my clients are broken.&lt;br/&gt;
So now we have to change our config files and code, or continue using&lt;br/&gt;
Configuration 1.0&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: Windows XP&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: PC&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342798">CONFIGURATION-59</key>

             }

             {&lt;br/&gt;

             {

         else&lt;br/&gt;
@@ -983,7 +984,7 @@&lt;/p&gt;
             {

-                array[0] = PropertyConverter.toFloat(value).intValue();

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-55] [configuration] Interpolation with multivalued keys returns nested strings instead of flattend string and interpolate doesn&apos;t work with all getters</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-55</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;I tried these properties with Configuration 1.1 stable (a&lt;br/&gt;
PropertiesConfiguration in a CompositeConfiguration, but that shouldn&apos;t matter)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;z=1,2,3,${x},7,8&lt;br/&gt;
x=4,${y}&lt;br/&gt;
y=5,6&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If queried using getStringArray(&quot;z&quot;) etc. this results in:&lt;br/&gt;
e.g. something like&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;String[] z = config.getStringArray(&quot;z&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
for (int i = 0; i &amp;lt; z.length; i++) {&lt;br/&gt;
  System.out.println(z&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;i&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;.toString());&lt;br/&gt;
}&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;1&lt;br/&gt;
2&lt;br/&gt;
3&lt;br/&gt;
[4, &lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;5, 6&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;]&lt;br/&gt;
7&lt;br/&gt;
8&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Note brackets and nesting!&lt;br/&gt;
I guess it would be better to flatten such multivalued keys without&lt;br/&gt;
brackets,commas and spaces e.g. the result should look like (note: this is&lt;br/&gt;
already formated a bit)&lt;br/&gt;
x = 4,5,6&lt;br/&gt;
y = 5,6&lt;br/&gt;
z = 1,2,3,4,5,6,7,8&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Also note that commons-configuration-src-20050926.zip nightly build behaves&lt;br/&gt;
different, here the result was (also preformated):&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;x = &lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;4, 5&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
y = &lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;5, 6&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
z = &lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;1, 2, 3, 4, 7, 8&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Looks as if only the first value is taken when interpolating...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8212;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Besides interpolate should get called for each getter.&lt;br/&gt;
a = ${b}&lt;br/&gt;
b = 5&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;One would expect config.getInt(&quot;a&quot;) == 5 instead of throwing an exception&lt;br/&gt;
because ${b} is no valid int. Of course, you can workaround by using&lt;br/&gt;
.getString(&quot;a&quot;) and converting manually, but this defeats the added value of all&lt;br/&gt;
different getters.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342577">CONFIGURATION-55</key>
            <summary>[configuration] Interpolation with multivalued keys returns nested strings instead of flattend string and interpolate doesn&apos;t work with all getters</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="5" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/resolved.png" description="A resolution has been taken, and it is awaiting verification by reporter. From here issues are either reopened, or are closed.">Resolved</status>

                            <comment id="12410459" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Tue, 27 Sep 2005 14:57:56 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;A while ago there was a discussion about interpolation of multi-valued&lt;br/&gt;
properties on the user list. The thread can be found here:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://mail-archives.apache.org/mod_mbox/jakarta-commons-user/200508.mbox/%3c20050817150058.1E260E04EE@gate2.excedent.us%3e&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://mail-archives.apache.org/mod_mbox/jakarta-commons-user/200508.mbox/%3c20050817150058.1E260E04EE@gate2.excedent.us%3e&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The outcome was this change in behavior you noticed and also the conclusion that&lt;br/&gt;
there is probably no correct solution to this problem because the expected&lt;br/&gt;
results strongly depend on a concrete use case.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It is planed to make interpolation support more configurable by allowing&lt;br/&gt;
customizable strategies. Interpolation support for other data types is on the&lt;br/&gt;
agenda, too. All these issues are covered in the bugzilla ticket 35116, so I am&lt;br/&gt;
marking this ticket as duplicate.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;
	&lt;ul&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;
		&lt;ul&gt;
			&lt;li&gt;This bug has been marked as a duplicate of 35116 ***&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;/ul&gt;
		&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;/ul&gt;
	&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
</comment>
                            <comment id="12410460" author="ebourg" created="Tue, 27 Sep 2005 19:16:55 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I think Michael has a point regarding getInt(&quot;a&quot;) throwing an exception in this&lt;br/&gt;
example. We could fix this easily before revamping the interpolation system:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;return PropertyConverter.toInteger(value);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;turns into&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;return PropertyConverter.toInteger(value instanceof String ?&lt;br/&gt;
interpolate((String) value) : value);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;for all getters in AbstractConfiguration and DataConfiguration.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410461" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Tue, 27 Sep 2005 20:24:57 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Then it would be easier to call interpolate() directly inside the&lt;br/&gt;
resolveContainerStore() method, which is invoked by all primitive getters.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410462" author="ebourg" created="Tue, 27 Sep 2005 21:12:42 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Interesting idea, I&apos;m not sure it&apos;s wise to overload the responsability of&lt;br/&gt;
resolveContainerStore() though. I have added an interpolate(Object) method that&lt;br/&gt;
returns the value as is if it&apos;s not a String. That makes the code shorter and&lt;br/&gt;
keeps it readable:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;return PropertyConverter.toInteger(interpolate(value));&lt;/p&gt;
</comment>
                            <comment id="12410463" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Tue, 27 Sep 2005 21:29:11 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;An Object interpolate(Object) method will be needed in future anyway, that&apos;s&lt;br/&gt;
fine with me.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;What resolveContainerStore() does ATM is to prepare a property value as far as&lt;br/&gt;
possible, so that primitive getters only need to perform a type conversion.&lt;br/&gt;
Performing interpolation is part of this task IMO. I would prefer having all&lt;br/&gt;
these steps at a central place to reduce code duplication.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;However &quot;resolveContainerStore&quot; is surely the wrong name for this method.&lt;br/&gt;
Because of backwards compatibility we cannot simply change the name. Should we&lt;br/&gt;
deprecate the method and instead introduce a new one with a better name?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410464" author="ebourg" created="Tue, 27 Sep 2005 21:53:24 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;My concern about interpolating in resolveContainerStore is that it will be only&lt;br/&gt;
useful for scalar getters (getInt(), getFloat()...) and not for list and array&lt;br/&gt;
getters, especially in DataConfiguration, which use getProperty(). That would&lt;br/&gt;
look a bit odd to call PropertyConverter.toInteger(value) in getInteger() and&lt;br/&gt;
PropertyConverter.toInteger(interpolate(value)) in getIntegerList(). One might&lt;br/&gt;
think by comparing the two methods that getInteger() doesn&apos;t not perform the&lt;br/&gt;
interpolation.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I agree that resolveContainerStore() is definitely not an explicit name. Its&lt;br/&gt;
logic could be moved in PropertyConverter as a toScalar(Object) or a&lt;br/&gt;
getHead(Object) method. Then we could remove resolveContainerStore() and call&lt;br/&gt;
directly the new method in PropertyConverter.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410465" author="ebourg" created="Tue, 27 Sep 2005 22:10:26 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I&apos;ve commited my changes introducing the new interpolate() method and performing&lt;br/&gt;
the interpolation in all getters.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                    </comments>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-54] [configuration] BaseConfiguration: containsKey ignores default properties</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-54</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;The current (CVS Head) implementation of BaseConfiguration.containsKey does not&lt;br/&gt;
check whether a key is contained in the &quot;defaults&quot; Configuration (if exists).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I think&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;public boolean containsKey(String key)&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        return store.containsKey(key);
    }

&lt;p&gt;should be:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;public boolean containsKey(String key)&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        return store.containsKey(key)
           || ((defaults != null) &amp;amp;&amp;amp; defaults.containsKey(key));
    }</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341246">CONFIGURATION-54</key>
            <summary>[configuration] BaseConfiguration: containsKey ignores default properties</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>

                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>

                            <comment id="12405935" author="christian@siefkes.net" created="Fri, 6 Feb 2004 02:42:21 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Of course, clearProperty(String key) must be adjusted as well when this is fixed.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;And shouldn&apos;t isEmpty() and getKeys() consider the &quot;defaults&quot; configuration too?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12405936" author="dep4b" created="Sun, 15 Feb 2004 02:56:36 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I have fixed this bug.  However I think maybe a refactoring of &lt;br/&gt;
AbstractConfiguration(Configuration defaults) is in order.  See email list&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12405937" author="christian@siefkes.net" created="Mon, 16 Feb 2004 21:47:34 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I&apos;m answering here because I&apos;m not subscribed to the list. I actually switched&lt;br/&gt;
from PropertiesConfiguration with default values to CompositeConfiguration after&lt;br/&gt;
discovering this bug.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;My initial reason for not using CompositeConfiguration was a documentation bug:&lt;br/&gt;
CompositeConfiguration.addProperty says &quot;CompositeConfigurations can not be&lt;br/&gt;
added to&quot;. Luckily, this isn&apos;t true (would have been a blocker for me if it&lt;br/&gt;
were), but I had to check the source code to find out.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Otherwise I&apos;m quite happy with using CompositeConfiguration instead of chained&lt;br/&gt;
defaults, but there is still one problem: CompositeConfiguration live in memory&lt;br/&gt;
only, I cannot store them. Currently I could convert a CompositeConfiguration to&lt;br/&gt;
a PropertiesConfiguration via the PropertiesConfiguration(Configuration&lt;br/&gt;
defaults) constructor for storing it, but if you remove the defaults that would&lt;br/&gt;
no longer be possible.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Is there another way for converting a CompositeConfiguration to a serializable&lt;br/&gt;
format, or could you add one? If yes, I think it a good idea to replace chained&lt;br/&gt;
defaults by CompositeConfiguration.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12405938" author="ebourg" created="Mon, 16 Feb 2004 22:10:15 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Maybe we could mark one of the configurations as the main configuration where&lt;br/&gt;
the added properties go instead of the in memory configuration. Then we might&lt;br/&gt;
add a save() method on the CompositeConfiguration that would call the save()&lt;br/&gt;
method on the contained configurations if available.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

            <title>[CONFIGURATION-53] [configuration] ConfigurationFactory does not merge configurations with the same structure</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-53</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Imagine conf1.xml and conf2.xml with the following content:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;conf1.xml:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
	&amp;lt;group name=&quot;name1&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;conf2.xml:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
	&amp;lt;group name=&quot;name2&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;when asking config.getList(&quot;group&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;@name&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&quot;), i would expect two elements in the&lt;br/&gt;
list, but I have only one (the one in the first config file included)&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

                            <comment id="12409747" author="ebourg" created="Sat, 9 Jul 2005 00:00:58 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Hi Fabien, the values of the properties are not merged unless you declare the&lt;br/&gt;
configurations in an &amp;lt;additional&amp;gt; block in the configuration descriptor. For&lt;br/&gt;
example:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;additional&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;xml fileName=&quot;conf1.xml&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;xml fileName=&quot;conf2.xml&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;/additional&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Did you use this syntax for your descriptor ?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-52] [configuration] &quot;extended properties&quot; still mentionned in javadocs</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-52</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;&quot;extended properties&quot; properties is still used in some files, for example in&lt;br/&gt;

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-50] [configuration] FileChangedReloadingStrategy fails to properly detect file change</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-50</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Two code examples that fail to detect / load file changes:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;=============================================================================Sample&lt;br/&gt;
1:  If properties file location is determined by searching the classpath,&lt;br/&gt;
changes are not detected.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;try {&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;PropertiesConfiguration propConfig = new&lt;br/&gt;
PropertiesConfiguration(&quot;commons.properties&quot;);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;FileChangedReloadingStrategy strategy = new FileChangedReloadingStrategy();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;strategy.setConfiguration(propConfig);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;strategy.setRefreshDelay(500);&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;strategy.init();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;for (;&lt;img class=&quot;emoticon&quot; src=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/emoticons/wink.png&quot; height=&quot;16&quot; width=&quot;16&quot; align=&quot;absmiddle&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
{

String prop1 = propConfig.getString(&quot;prop1&quot;);

System.out.println(Calendar.getInstance().getTime() + &quot; : &quot; +
strategy.reloadingRequired() + &quot; : &quot; + prop1);

Thread.sleep(1000);

}


&lt;p&gt;} catch (Throwable t)&lt;/p&gt;
{

t.printStackTrace();

}&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
=============================================================================&lt;br/&gt;
Sample 2:  If properties file location is specified, changes are not detected&lt;br/&gt;
but not loaded.&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
try {&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
PropertiesConfiguration propConfig = new&lt;br/&gt;
PropertiesConfiguration(&quot;d:/tmp/commons.properties&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
FileChangedReloadingStrategy strategy = new FileChangedReloadingStrategy();&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
strategy.setConfiguration(propConfig);&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
strategy.setRefreshDelay(500);&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
strategy.init();&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
for (;;){

String prop1 = propConfig.getString(&quot;prop1&quot;);

System.out.println(Calendar.getInstance().getTime() + &quot; : &quot; +
strategy.reloadingRequired() + &quot; : &quot; + prop1);

Thread.sleep(1000);

}&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
} catch (Throwable t){
t.printStackTrace();
}</description>

            <summary>[configuration] FileChangedReloadingStrategy fails to properly detect file change</summary>

                            <comment id="12409020" author="ebourg" created="Mon, 4 Apr 2005 23:21:26 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Hi Eric, could you try again by setting the strategy on the configuration&lt;br/&gt;
instead of setting the configuration on the strategy ?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;FileConfiguration conf = new PropertiesConfiguration(&quot;commons.properties&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
conf.setReloadingStrategy(new FileChangedReloadingStrategy());&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409021" author="eric.lee@genworth.com" created="Tue, 5 Apr 2005 00:32:20 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Setting the strategy on the configuration instead of setting the configuration &lt;br/&gt;
on the strategy solves Sample #2, but does not solve Sample #1 (properties &lt;br/&gt;
file location is determined by searching the classpath).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;===========================================================================&lt;br/&gt;
PropertiesConfiguration propConfig = new PropertiesConfiguration&lt;br/&gt;
(&quot;commons.properties&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
FileChangedReloadingStrategy strategy = new FileChangedReloadingStrategy();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;strategy.setConfiguration(propConfig);&lt;br/&gt;
strategy.setRefreshDelay(500);&lt;br/&gt;
strategy.init();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;propConfig.setReloadingStrategy(strategy);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;for (;&lt;img class=&quot;emoticon&quot; src=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/emoticons/wink.png&quot; height=&quot;16&quot; width=&quot;16&quot; align=&quot;absmiddle&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;{&lt;br/&gt;
	String prop1 = propConfig.getString(&quot;prop1&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
	System.out.println(Calendar.getInstance().getTime() + &quot; : &quot; + &lt;br/&gt;
strategy.reloadingRequired() + &quot; : &quot; + prop1);&lt;br/&gt;
	Thread.sleep(1000);&lt;br/&gt;
}&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409022" author="ebourg" created="Tue, 5 Apr 2005 02:24:19 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;The strategy is already initialized by the configuration when&lt;br/&gt;
setReloadingStrategy is called, you don&apos;t need to call&lt;br/&gt;
strategy.setConfiguration() nor strategy.init().&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Also I don&apos;t think this is the best example to test the strategy. Since the call&lt;br/&gt;
to getString() will generate a call to reloadingPerformed() if the file changed,&lt;br/&gt;
calling reloadingRequired() after that will return &quot;false&quot; most of the time,&lt;br/&gt;
unless the file changed between the two instructions.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So I suggest you try this instead:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;PropertiesConfiguration config= new PropertiesConfiguration(&quot;commons.properties&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
FileChangedReloadingStrategy strategy = new FileChangedReloadingStrategy();&lt;br/&gt;
strategy.setRefreshDelay(500);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;config.setReloadingStrategy(strategy);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;for (;&lt;img class=&quot;emoticon&quot; src=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/emoticons/wink.png&quot; height=&quot;16&quot; width=&quot;16&quot; align=&quot;absmiddle&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot;/&gt;{&lt;br/&gt;
	System.out.println((new Date()) + &quot; : &quot; + strategy.reloadingRequired() + &quot; : &quot;&lt;br/&gt;
+ config.getString(&quot;prop1&quot;));&lt;br/&gt;
	Thread.sleep(1000);&lt;br/&gt;
}&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409023" author="eric.lee@genworth.com" created="Tue, 5 Apr 2005 11:56:37 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;The latest example exposes another bug...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If the fully qualified properties file name is specified:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;PropertiesConfiguration config= new PropertiesConfiguration&lt;br/&gt;
(&quot;d:/tmp/commons.properties&quot;);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;and the ouput statement is:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;System.out.println((new Date()) + &quot; : &quot; + strategy.reloadingRequired() + &quot; : &quot;&lt;br/&gt;
+ config.getString(&quot;prop1&quot;));&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The updated propery is not retrieved.  It appears that &lt;br/&gt;
strategy.reloadingRequired() sets a flag and the next property retrieval &lt;br/&gt;
request does not actaully reload the file.  Commenting out &lt;br/&gt;
strategy.reloadingRequired() allows the updated property to be reloaded.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;When only the file name is suppled and the file is loaded from a location in &lt;br/&gt;
the classpath, commenting out strategy.reloadingRequired()  still does not &lt;br/&gt;
cause the updated property to be reloaded, e.g.:  &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;PropertiesConfiguration config= new PropertiesConfiguration&lt;br/&gt;
(&quot;commons.properties&quot;);&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;The problem appears to be caused by the basePath member of &lt;br/&gt;
AbstractFileConfiguration not getting set properly after the properties file &lt;br/&gt;
URL is obtained from the classpath.  I was able to correct the problem by &lt;br/&gt;
modifying AbstractFileConfiguration.load(String) from:&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;    public void load(String fileName) throws ConfigurationException&lt;br/&gt;
    {&lt;br/&gt;
        try&lt;br/&gt;
        {&lt;br/&gt;
            URL url = ConfigurationUtils.locate(basePath, fileName);&lt;br/&gt;
            if (url == null)&lt;/p&gt;
            {
                throw new ConfigurationException(&quot;Cannot locate configuration 
source &quot; + fileName);
            }&lt;br/&gt;
            load(url);&lt;br/&gt;
        }&lt;br/&gt;
        catch (ConfigurationException e)&lt;br/&gt;
        {
            throw e;
        }&lt;br/&gt;
        catch (Exception e)&lt;br/&gt;
        {
            throw new ConfigurationException(e.getMessage(), e);
        }&lt;br/&gt;
    }&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
to: &lt;br/&gt;
&lt;br/&gt;
    public void load(String fileName) throws ConfigurationException&lt;br/&gt;
    {&lt;br/&gt;
        try&lt;br/&gt;
        {&lt;br/&gt;
            URL url = ConfigurationUtils.locate(basePath, fileName);&lt;br/&gt;
            if (url == null)&lt;br/&gt;
            {                throw new ConfigurationException(&quot;Cannot locate configuration source &quot; + fileName);            }
&lt;p&gt;            if(null == basePath)&lt;/p&gt;
{
            	setFile(new File(url.getFile()));
            }
&lt;p&gt;            load(url);&lt;br/&gt;
        }&lt;br/&gt;
        catch (ConfigurationException e)&lt;/p&gt;
        {
            throw e;
        }
&lt;p&gt;        catch (Exception e)&lt;/p&gt;
        {
            throw new ConfigurationException(e.getMessage(), e);
        }
&lt;p&gt;    }&lt;/p&gt;
</comment>
                            <comment id="12409024" author="eric.lee@genworth.com" created="Fri, 13 May 2005 22:15:50 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Are there any plans to fix this bug?  If so what is the target milestone / date?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Thx,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Eric.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409025" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Sun, 22 May 2005 00:51:20 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=15105)&lt;br/&gt;
Patch for FileChangedReloadingStrategy including unit test&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This is a patch which should solve the problem. The idea is that the reloading&lt;br/&gt;
strategy no longer uses configuration.getFile() to obtain a file reference, but&lt;br/&gt;
relies on configuration.getURL(), which should (in most cases) point to the&lt;br/&gt;
correct file.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Eric, can you verify if this works for you?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Emmanuel, could you pleas double check? This patch should solve issue 34376,&lt;br/&gt;
too.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409026" author="jorge.ferrer@gmail.com" created="Sun, 22 May 2005 17:19:46 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=15115)&lt;br/&gt;
Add method containerFileURL to be used by FileChangedReloadingStrategy&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I suggest adding a method called containerFileFromURL which converts the&lt;br/&gt;
specified URL to a file object which points to a file in the file system. If&lt;br/&gt;
the URL points directly to a file in the file system the returned object will&lt;br/&gt;
point to it, on the other side if it points to a file inside a JAR the returned&lt;br/&gt;
file object will point to the JAR file. If this fails, &amp;lt;b&amp;gt;null&amp;lt;/b&amp;gt; is returned.&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;The original fileFromURL cannot be modified because it is used by&lt;br/&gt;
AbstractFileConfiguration and it expects to get be returned a file which the&lt;br/&gt;
configuration can be saved to.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409027" author="jorge.ferrer@gmail.com" created="Sun, 22 May 2005 17:29:25 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=15116)&lt;br/&gt;
Substitute for FileChangedReloadingStrategy which solves the problem for&lt;br/&gt;
Configuration 1.1&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This class can be used as a replacement of FileChangedReloadingStrategy until a&lt;br/&gt;
version of Configuration which solves this bug is released.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409028" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Tue, 31 May 2005 19:29:41 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Created an attachment (id=15228)&lt;br/&gt;
Updated patch for FileChangedReloadingStrategy plus unit test&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Patch updated to incorporate changes suggested by Jorge Ferrer.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;FileChangedReloadingStrategy will now correctly update its lastChanged field,&lt;br/&gt;
so that hasChanged() need not be called every time reloadingRequired() is&lt;br/&gt;
invoked.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I also included the proposed functionality that if a configuration file is&lt;br/&gt;
loaded from a jar, the jar file itself should be the target for the strategy.&lt;br/&gt;
However IMO the containerFileURL() method seems to be very specific to the&lt;br/&gt;
reloading strategy, so I placed the code directly in&lt;br/&gt;
FileChangedReloadingStrategy. If we later find out that this stuff is generally&lt;br/&gt;
useful, we can still move it to ConfigurationUtils and make it public.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409029" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Tue, 31 May 2005 19:37:57 +0000"  >&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;
	&lt;ul&gt;

            <title>[CONFIGURATION-49] [configuration] XMLConfiguration may lose attributes in its save() method</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-49</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Under some circumstances (if a configuration is loaded, cleared and then&lt;br/&gt;
reloaded), the save() method forgets to write attributes. Their values are still&lt;br/&gt;
contained in the configuration object itself, but they are not written to the&lt;br/&gt;
output file.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

            <title>[CONFIGURATION-48] [configuration] ReloadingStrategy with Classpath file</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-48</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Hello&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;First of all, congratulation for your incredible job.&lt;br/&gt;
I have tested commons-configuration with a properties file find in the&lt;br/&gt;
user-Classpath. This PropertiesConfiguration has a FileChangedReloadingStrategy.&lt;br/&gt;
When this file is changed, the protected method hasChanged() from the&lt;br/&gt;
FileChangedReloadingStrategy class stucks on the &quot;if&lt;br/&gt;
(!configuration.getFile().exists())&quot; line. The file never exists !!!&lt;br/&gt;
I have change the AbstractFileConfiguration class by affected to a protected&lt;br/&gt;
propertie fileUrl the URL in the &quot;public void load(String fileName)&quot; method.&lt;br/&gt;
After, I&apos;ve changed the getFile  : &lt;br/&gt;
public File getFile()&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        //HGerard - MACIF
        return ConfigurationUtils.fileFromURL(this.fileUrl);
        //return ConfigurationUtils.getFile(getBasePath(), getFileName());
    }

&lt;p&gt;and it works. Is this a bug or i don&apos;t understand how to use the&lt;br/&gt;
PropertiesConfiguration ?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;best regards.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Herve GERARD&lt;/p&gt;</description>
