<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-47] [configuration] ConfigurationFactory loading from classpath issue</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-47</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;I found a thread on the commons mailing list about this topic, but did not see a&lt;br/&gt;
resolution presented.  &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.mail-archive.com/commons-user@jakarta.apache.org/msg07782.html&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://www.mail-archive.com/commons-user@jakarta.apache.org/msg07782.html&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It seems the only way to load a properties file from a separate jar in the&lt;br/&gt;
classpath is to use absolute paths.  I believe the ConfigurationFactory&lt;br/&gt;
framework would be a tad more useful if it used the classloader to load the&lt;br/&gt;
properties files as resources instead.  The major advantage being that one could&lt;br/&gt;
package a default properties file in a config jar, but temporarily override it&lt;br/&gt;
by placing a copy higher in the classpath.  There are other uses as well, but&lt;br/&gt;
that&apos;s the main use case I have in mind right now.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Let&apos;s say I have the following JAR that contains only these configuration files:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;core-config&lt;br/&gt;
  properties/config.xml  &amp;lt;= The ConfigurationFactory settings&lt;br/&gt;
  properties/test-config.xml  &amp;lt;= An XML properties file&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;core-configtest&lt;br/&gt;
  com.test.ConfigurationTest &amp;lt;= Constructs ConfigurationFactory and calls&lt;br/&gt;
getConfiguration()&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Because I use the classload to load &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;!-- config.xml --&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;xml fileName=&quot;test-config.xml&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I have tried many variations of the above path to get it to load from the&lt;br/&gt;
classpath to no avail, such as:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;xml fileName=&quot;properties/test-config.xml&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;xml fileName=&quot;/properties/test-config.xml&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;xml fileName=&quot;file:test-config.xml&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;xml fileName=&quot;file:properties/test-config.xml&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;xml fileName=&quot;file:/properties/test-config.xml&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Most of the time it coughs out a SAXException with a garbled path like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Could not load from&lt;br/&gt;
C:\dev\Java\Core-ConfigTest\&lt;a href=&quot;file:C:devJavaCore-ConfigTestlibcore-config.jar!propertiestest-config.xml&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;file:\C:\dev\Java\Core-ConfigTest\lib\core-config.jar!\properties\test-config.xml&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.commons.digester.Digester.createSAXException(Digester.java:2540)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.commons.digester.Digester.createSAXException(Digester.java:2566)&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.commons.digester.Digester.endElement(Digester.java:1061)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In other words, I can&apos;t seem to make it use the appropriate URL for accessing&lt;br/&gt;
the file when it&apos;s in another JAR.  &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;jar:&lt;a href=&quot;file:/C:/dev/Java/Core-ConfigTest/lib/core-config.jar!/properties/config.xml&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;file:/C:/dev/Java/Core-ConfigTest/lib/core-config.jar!/properties/config.xml&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If I move the properties folder to the JAR that contains the test class, it&lt;br/&gt;
works fine.  I believe I could also use an absolute path to the properties file,&lt;br/&gt;
but again, that precludes me from being able to quickly override the properties&lt;br/&gt;
file by placing a copy higher in the classpath.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This is my first experience with trying to initiate a change in an open source&lt;br/&gt;
project, so bear with me if I&apos;m not following the right protocol.  I&apos;d like to&lt;br/&gt;
take a stab at creating a patch myself if someone hasn&apos;t already beat me to it.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Thanks.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341659">CONFIGURATION-47</key>

            <title>[CONFIGURATION-46] [Configuration] Documentation Issue</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-46</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;I think there&apos;s an error in the documentation for commons-configuration &lt;br/&gt;
examples page.&lt;br/&gt;
If I use this example:&lt;br/&gt;
   ConfigurationFactory factory = new ConfigurationFactory();&lt;br/&gt;
   URL configURL = getClass().getResource(&quot;/config.xml&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
   factory.setConfigurationFileName(configURL.toString());&lt;br/&gt;
   Configuration config = factory.getConfiguration();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I get a NPE, but if I change to this:&lt;br/&gt;
  ConfigurationFactory factory = new ConfigurationFactory();&lt;br/&gt;
  URL configURL = getClass().getResource(&quot;/config.xml&quot;);&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul class=&quot;alternate&quot; type=&quot;square&quot;&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;factory.setConfigurationFileName(configURL.toString());&lt;br/&gt;
+ factory.setConfigurationFileName(configURL.getFile());&lt;br/&gt;
  Configuration config = factory.getConfiguration();&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;everthing is fine. Basically, the setConfigFileName in ConfigurationFactory is &lt;br/&gt;
not expecting a URI its expecting a path i think?&lt;/p&gt;</description>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-45] [configuration] Fails silently if asked to save to an invalid filename</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-45</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Running code like this...&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;FileConfiguration config = new PropertiesConfiguration();&lt;br/&gt;
config.setFile(new File(&quot;/invalid/path/my.properties&quot;));&lt;br/&gt;
config.save();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;...doesn&apos;t throw any Exception. AbstractFileConfiguration.save(File) swallows &lt;br/&gt;
the FileNotFoundException, prints a stack trace, and completes normally, &lt;br/&gt;
without having saved the file.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Cheers&lt;br/&gt;
Iain Shepherd&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341848">CONFIGURATION-45</key>
            <summary>[configuration] Fails silently if asked to save to an invalid filename</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="apache.org@ishepherd.co.uk">Iain Shepherd</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Tue, 2 Nov 2004 22:44:37 +0000</created>
                <updated>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:39 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:39 +0000</resolved>
                                    <version>1.0</version>
                                    <fixVersion>1.1</fixVersion>
                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12407944" author="ebourg" created="Mon, 15 Nov 2004 21:02:28 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;What&apos;s the best solution ? Throwing a ConfigurationException wrapping the&lt;br/&gt;
FileNotFoundException, or creating the path and the file automatically ?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407945" author="apache.org@ishepherd.co.uk" created="Mon, 15 Nov 2004 21:16:46 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;&amp;gt; Throwing a ConfigurationException wrapping the&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; FileNotFoundException, or creating the path and the file automatically ?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Just IMO, creating the file would be good - but not always possible. The path &lt;br/&gt;
might be completely invalid or on a drive that isn&apos;t present etc. In which case &lt;br/&gt;
you&apos;d have to throw.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407946" author="ebourg" created="Fri, 19 Nov 2004 20:36:13 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;-&amp;gt; Taking the bug&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12407947" author="ebourg" created="Fri, 19 Nov 2004 20:50:37 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I&apos;m going to change AbstractFileConfiguration in order to have a consistent&lt;br/&gt;
behaviour with the following operations:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;(1) FileConfiguration config = new FileConfiguration(file);&lt;br/&gt;
    config.save();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;(2) FileConfiguration config = new FileConfiguration();&lt;br/&gt;
    config.setFile(file);&lt;br/&gt;
    config.save();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;(3) FileConfiguration config = new FileConfiguration();&lt;br/&gt;
    config.save(file);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In all 3 cases, the file will be created when the configuration is saved. For&lt;br/&gt;
(1) this implies the configuration is loaded only if the file exists, the&lt;br/&gt;
ConfigurationException will no longer be thrown if the file doesn&apos;t exist. (3)&lt;br/&gt;
is slightly different because it doesn&apos;t change the file associated with the&lt;br/&gt;
configuration, this will not change.&lt;/p&gt;



&lt;ul class=&quot;alternate&quot; type=&quot;square&quot;&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
</comment>
                            <comment id="12407948" author="ebourg" created="Fri, 19 Nov 2004 22:21:42 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Changes applied, save(File) also throws an exception when an error occurs now.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-44] [configuration] Composite configuration with JNDI logs failed access as ERROR</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-44</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;This is a report from the Turbine developer list.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Commons configuration 1.1 logs failed JNDI lookups at ERROR level. I use the&lt;br/&gt;
composite configuration as follows&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;jndi prefix=&quot;java:comp/env&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;properties fileName=&quot;WEB-INF/conf/TurbineResources.properties&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;This configuration is described in the configuration-howto of Turbine.&lt;br/&gt;
The expected behaviour is that the entries in the JNDI context overwrite those&lt;br/&gt;
in the properties file. That, in turn, means, that usually only a few&lt;br/&gt;
configuration keys will exist in the JNDI context.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In the current version of commons-configuration (1.1) this means an error entry&lt;br/&gt;
in the log with every access to a not overridden configuration key (which are&lt;br/&gt;
the majority).&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Could you please reduce the log level for this or return to the behaviour of&lt;br/&gt;
version 1.0 not to log this at all?&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342554">CONFIGURATION-44</key>
            <summary>[configuration] Composite configuration with JNDI logs failed access as ERROR</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="tv">Thomas Vandahl</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Thu, 15 Sep 2005 15:49:46 +0000</created>
                <updated>Tue, 16 May 2006 12:09:49 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Tue, 16 May 2006 12:09:49 +0000</resolved>
                                    <version>1.1</version>
                                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12410400" author="ebourg" created="Thu, 15 Sep 2005 17:02:00 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Good point, missing properties in the JNDI context shouldn&apos;t be logged as&lt;br/&gt;
errors, but it is desirable to log the other errors. What exception is really&lt;br/&gt;
thrown by Context.lookup ? Is it a NameNotFoundException, or just a&lt;br/&gt;
NamingException as documented in the javadoc ? If the implementation throws a&lt;br/&gt;
NameNotFoundException we could remove the logging for this case and keep it for&lt;br/&gt;
the other errors.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410401" author="tv" created="Thu, 15 Sep 2005 17:12:29 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;The stacktrace is as follows:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;2005-09-15 10:08:52,015 ERROR&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;org.apache.commons.configuration.JNDIConfiguration&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt; Name log4j is not bound in&lt;br/&gt;
this Context&lt;br/&gt;
javax.naming.NameNotFoundException: Name log4j is not bound in this Context&lt;br/&gt;
	at org.apache.naming.NamingContext.lookup(NamingContext.java:814)&lt;br/&gt;

	at&lt;br/&gt;

	at&lt;br/&gt;
org.apache.commons.configuration.CompositeConfiguration.getProperty(CompositeConfiguration.java:152)&lt;br/&gt;
	at&lt;br/&gt;

	at&lt;br/&gt;

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-43] [configuration] BaseConfiguration.addProperty() and MapConfiguration.addProperty() do not behave the same</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-43</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Hello,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;the contract of Configuration.addProperty(), namely to add the value to the list&lt;br/&gt;
of values for that property, is not held by MapConfiguration.addProperty() where&lt;br/&gt;
the previous value is simply replaced by the new one.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Example 1 with a BaseConfiguration (OK):&lt;br/&gt;
conf = new BaseConfiguration();&lt;br/&gt;
conf.addProperty( &quot;key&quot;, &quot;value1&quot; ); // &quot;key&quot; --&amp;gt; &quot;value1&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
conf.addProperty( &quot;key&quot;, &quot;value2&quot; ); // &quot;key&quot; --&amp;gt; [ &quot;value1&quot;, &quot;value2&quot; ]&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Example 2 with a MapConfiguration (BAD):&lt;br/&gt;
conf = new BaseConfiguration();&lt;br/&gt;
conf.addProperty( &quot;key&quot;, &quot;value1&quot; ); // &quot;key&quot; --&amp;gt; &quot;value1&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
conf.addProperty( &quot;key&quot;, &quot;value2&quot; ); // &quot;key&quot; --&amp;gt; &quot;value2&quot; : CONTRACT NOT RESPECTED!&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342750">CONFIGURATION-43</key>
            <summary>[configuration] BaseConfiguration.addProperty() and MapConfiguration.addProperty() do not behave the same</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>

                            <comment id="12410955" author="smarc@gmx.net" created="Tue, 29 Nov 2005 15:54:15 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;(In reply to comment #0)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;little correction, should read:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;gt; Example 1 with a BaseConfiguration (OK):&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; conf1 = new BaseConfiguration();&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; conf1.addProperty( &quot;key&quot;, &quot;value1&quot; ); // &quot;key&quot; --&amp;gt; &quot;value1&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; conf1.addProperty( &quot;key&quot;, &quot;value2&quot; ); // &quot;key&quot; --&amp;gt; [ &quot;value1&quot;, &quot;value2&quot; ]&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; &lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; Example 2 with a MapConfiguration (BAD):&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; conf2 = new MapConfiguration( new HashMap() );&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; conf2.addProperty( &quot;key&quot;, &quot;value1&quot; ); // &quot;key&quot; --&amp;gt; &quot;value1&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; conf2.addProperty( &quot;key&quot;, &quot;value2&quot; ); // &quot;key&quot; --&amp;gt; &quot;value2&quot; : CONTRACT NOT&lt;br/&gt;
RESPECTED!&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410956" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Tue, 29 Nov 2005 21:39:46 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Looking at the source of MapConfiguration properties with multiple values seem&lt;br/&gt;
to be treated correctly.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;To be sure I ran the following test case:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public void testAddProperty()&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        Configuration config = new MapConfiguration(new HashMap());
        config.addProperty(&quot;key&quot;, &quot;value1&quot;);
        config.addProperty(&quot;key&quot;, &quot;value2&quot;);
        assertEquals(&quot;Property has only a single value&quot;, 2,
config.getList(&quot;key&quot;).size());
    }

&lt;p&gt;This works for me. So, could you please double check? Or didn&apos;t I understand&lt;br/&gt;
your problem correctly?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410957" author="smarc@gmx.net" created="Fri, 2 Dec 2005 23:40:13 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I created the same test as you (copy/paste) and the assertion failed: size()&lt;br/&gt;
returns 1. As I tried to explain it in the bug description, adding properties to&lt;br/&gt;
existing values simply overwrites the preceeding ones.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I had a look at the code: AbstractConfiguration defines addProperty() which&lt;br/&gt;
calls the abstract addPropertyDirect(), which in turn is implemented in&lt;br/&gt;
MapConfiguration as follows:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    protected void addPropertyDirect(String key, Object obj)&lt;/p&gt;
    {
        map.put(key, obj);
    }

&lt;p&gt;As Map.put() overwrites any existing values, the contract of addProperty is not&lt;br/&gt;
respected.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I downloaded the binaries and sources from the apache website, current the&lt;br/&gt;
version is 1.1.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So as it is working for you, I decided to look at the SVN version. The code for&lt;br/&gt;
addPropertyDirect seems to be better up there:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    protected void addPropertyDirect(String key, Object value)&lt;br/&gt;
    {&lt;br/&gt;
        Object previousValue = getProperty(key);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        if (previousValue == null)&lt;/p&gt;
        {
            map.put(key, value);
        }
&lt;p&gt;        else if (previousValue instanceof List)&lt;/p&gt;
        {
            // the value is added to the existing list
            ((List) previousValue).add(value);
        }
&lt;p&gt;        else&lt;/p&gt;
        {
            // the previous value is replaced by a list containing the previous
value and the new value
            List list = new ArrayList();
            list.add(previousValue);
            list.add(value);

            map.put(key, list);
        }
&lt;p&gt;    }&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So I think the bug I&apos;m describing has been fixed, but is not currently available&lt;br/&gt;
in the latest release... When is the next release planned for?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410958" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Sat, 3 Dec 2005 00:30:57 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;We are in the process of getting the next release out. You can find the latest&lt;br/&gt;
release candidate here:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://people.apache.org/~oheger/commons-configuration-1.2RC2/&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://people.apache.org/~oheger/commons-configuration-1.2RC2/&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;(Your issue should have been fixed in this version.)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;If there are no unexpected issues, commons-configuration 1.2 final should be&lt;br/&gt;
available really soon now. There won&apos;t be much difference to the release&lt;br/&gt;
candidate mentioned above.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Okay, I am closing this ticket now.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

            <title>[CONFIGURATION-42] [configuration] HeirarchicalXML save unsupported not documented</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-42</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;It should be documented that the HeirachicalXML.save method will throw an&lt;br/&gt;
UnsupportedOperationException&lt;br/&gt;
When choosing the apache commons configuration classes, I was specifically&lt;br/&gt;
looking for a way to load and save configurations.&lt;br/&gt;
Having read the howto&apos;s on the main site and the javadoc for&lt;br/&gt;
HeirachicalXMLConfiguration, it is not indicated anywhere that this class does&lt;br/&gt;
not support being saved, which is counter intuitive since it has a save method.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The javadoc for this class should clearly state that the save operations do not&lt;br/&gt;
work.&lt;br/&gt;
It would also be desirable for the superclass&apos;s declaration of save to note that&lt;br/&gt;
it is possible that some subclasses may throw an UnsupportedOperationException&lt;/p&gt;</description>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-41] [configuration] Output format of FileConfiguration classes</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-41</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;I am using Commons Configuration 1.1.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Saving &apos;FielConfiguration&apos;s the configuration files will be overwritten every time.&lt;br/&gt;
Bad if you have formatted them with descriptions and comments ... but this is&lt;br/&gt;
not so important.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Not so good is, that in the class:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;PropertiesConfiguration:&lt;br/&gt;
&apos;\n&apos; is used as &quot;line separator&quot; and not the &quot;System.getProperty(&quot;line.separator&quot;)&quot;.&lt;br/&gt;
So, on Windows systems the configuration files are badly readable.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;XMLConfiguration:&lt;br/&gt;
The encoding is not looped though to the encoding in the XML head declaration.&lt;br/&gt;
Every time &quot;UTF-8&quot; is set (&amp;lt;?xml version=&quot;1.0&quot; encoding=&quot;UTF-8&quot;?&amp;gt;)&lt;br/&gt;
I would prefer that my encoding (setEncoding()) is reflected in the XML document.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Is there a reason that it is implemented like you do?&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Attached are patches which would resolve the problems (if you want):&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;PropertiesConfiguration.java:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;properties_lineseparator.patch&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;136a137,138&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt;     private static final String lineSeparator =&lt;br/&gt;
System.getProperty(&quot;line.separator&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt; &lt;br/&gt;
344c346&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;                 out.write(&quot;\n&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;#8212;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt;                 out.write(lineSeparator);&lt;br/&gt;
349c351&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;             out.write(&quot;\n&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;#8212;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt;             out.write(lineSeparator);&lt;br/&gt;
486c488&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;             write(&apos;\n&apos;);&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;#8212;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt;             write(lineSeparator);&lt;br/&gt;
511c513&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;             write(&quot;# &quot; + comment + &quot;\n&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;#8212;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt;             write(&quot;# &quot; + comment + lineSeparator);&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;XMLConfiguration.java:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;XML_encoding.patch&lt;br/&gt;
446a447&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;gt;             transformer.setOutputProperty(OutputKeys.ENCODING, getEncoding());&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: Windows 2000&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342663">CONFIGURATION-41</key>
            <summary>[configuration] Output format of FileConfiguration classes</summary>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-40] [configuration] subset() method alters XMLConfiguration when invoked</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-40</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Invoking subset() on an XMLConfiguration causes the underlying hierarchy to &lt;br/&gt;
change.  For example, using the database example on the webpage, performing &lt;br/&gt;
the following and then serializing the XMLConfiguration file will show the &lt;br/&gt;
structure has been altered:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;XMLConfiguration xmlConfig = new XMLConfiguration(databaseDotXmlUrl);&lt;br/&gt;
xmlConfig.subset(&quot;tables.table(0&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
xmlConfig.save(&quot;C:/AlteredDatabase.xml&quot;);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Not sure this was the intent of the method... actually the method returns a &lt;br/&gt;
new HierarchicalConfiguration object but this method has undesired side effect &lt;br/&gt;
on the original configuration.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: Windows XP&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: PC&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-39] [configuration] FileChangedReloadingStrategy javadoc misleading</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-39</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;The current javadoc for 1.1 version of Configuration is as follows:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A reloading strategy that will reload the configuration every time its underlying file is changed. The file &lt;br/&gt;
is not reloaded more than once every 5 seconds by default, this time can be changed by setting the &lt;br/&gt;
refresh delay. This strategy only works with FileConfiguration instances.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I was under the false impression that a thread would be created which would periodically wake up every &lt;br/&gt;
5 seconds and poll the property file to see if it has changed or not. If the file has changed then it would &lt;br/&gt;
be reloaded. However this is not the case. After diving into the code, you need to call one of the get*() &lt;br/&gt;
methods (i.e. getInt(), getLong(), etc...) before the file is checked.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Finally, it would be nice to have some kind of callback mechanism to notify listeners that implement a &lt;br/&gt;
well known interface defined in the configuration API that the file has changed.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Thanks for all your hard work!&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342341">CONFIGURATION-39</key>
            <summary>[configuration] FileChangedReloadingStrategy javadoc misleading</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="5" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/trivial.svg">Trivial</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="jnikolai@is2inc.com">John Nikolai</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Wed, 29 Jun 2005 05:47:30 +0000</created>
                <updated>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:39 +0000</updated>

                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12409693" author="ebourg" created="Wed, 29 Jun 2005 09:00:36 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Hi John, thank you for the feedback, we&apos;ll try to make the javadoc less&lt;br/&gt;
ambiguous. The notification mechanism is a topic that is still being discussed&lt;br/&gt;
(see &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-204&quot; title=&quot;Periodic reloading&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;CONFIGURATION-204&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;COM-2174&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), suggestions and contributions are much welcome in this area.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409694" author="jnikolai@is2inc.com" created="Wed, 29 Jun 2005 09:26:05 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Thanks for the response... I will have a look at &lt;a href=&quot;https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-204&quot; title=&quot;Periodic reloading&quot; class=&quot;issue-link&quot; data-issue-key=&quot;CONFIGURATION-204&quot;&gt;&lt;del&gt;COM-2174&lt;/del&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Would there be an interest in creating a new class that would maintain a thread which in turn would &lt;br/&gt;
periodically wake and check the status of the watched file? This could work wonderfully with the &lt;br/&gt;
notification mechanism.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409695" author="jordanh@zootweb.com" created="Tue, 23 Aug 2005 00:30:28 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Spawning a thread would probably violate the j2ee spec and cause huge problems&lt;br/&gt;
for people who use containers like JBoss.  Having a true monitoring solution&lt;br/&gt;
would be really nice though. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;What does the 5000 ms rate actually do if not monitor the file every 5 seconds?&lt;br/&gt;
 I to found the javadoc incredibly confusing.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409696" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Mon, 29 Aug 2005 03:27:19 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I changed the class comment for FileChangedReloadingStrategy so that it now&lt;br/&gt;
hopefully better describes the function of this class. If there are better&lt;br/&gt;
suggestions, please reopen and attach.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-35] [configuration] PropertiesConfiguration.load should default to encoding &quot;8859_1&quot;</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-35</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Same issue as:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://issues.apache.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=17616&quot; class=&quot;external-link&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;http://issues.apache.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=17616&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Copied from 17616&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The default load method for commons.collections.ExtendedProperties currently &lt;br/&gt;
loads properties using the default JVM encoding.  The default load() method &lt;br/&gt;
should use &quot;8859_1&quot; encoding.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Rationale:&lt;br/&gt;
1) consistency: java.util.Properties.load() method always uses &quot;8859_1&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
2) properties resources are always 8859_1, by convention.&lt;br/&gt;
2) On edbcic machines, particularly IBM mainframes, the default encoding is &lt;br/&gt;
Cp1047 (ebcdic), but properties files are always ASCII (ISO8859-1)&lt;br/&gt;
3) This bug causes many Apache tools, such as Velocity, which uses &lt;br/&gt;
commons.collections, to fail on non-ascii machines, since they distribute &lt;br/&gt;
properties resources which are (correctly) in 8859-1.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342559">CONFIGURATION-35</key>
            <summary>[configuration] PropertiesConfiguration.load should default to encoding &quot;8859_1&quot;</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-34] [configuration] XMLConfiguration.addProperty doesn&apos;t create new child nodes</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-34</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;Issue reported by Ben Hutchison on the dev list:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;XMLConfiguration.addProperty(key, Object) doesn&apos;t handle nest keys&lt;br/&gt;
properly.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;In this loop logic, the full key name is broken into parts, and the DOM&lt;br/&gt;
tree is walked. However, if a branch mentioned in the key isn&apos;t there,&lt;br/&gt;
the loop incorrectly breaks out. Result is that eg addProperty(&quot;a.b&quot;)&lt;br/&gt;
doesn&apos;t actually add at &quot;a.b&quot; unless &quot;a&quot; &amp;amp; &quot;b&quot; already exist. Old&lt;br/&gt;
version shown:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        String[] nodes = parseElementNames(name);&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;        Element element = document.getDocumentElement();&lt;br/&gt;
        Element parent = element;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        for (int i = 0; i &amp;lt; nodes.length; i++) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            if (element == null)
                break;    //******************** this is not right
**********************
            parent = element;
            String eName = nodes[i];
            Element child = getChildElementWithName(eName, element);

            element = child;
        }

&lt;p&gt;My tested fix:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        Element element = document.getDocumentElement();&lt;br/&gt;
        Element child = null;&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;        for (int i = 0; i &amp;lt; nodes.length; i++) {&lt;br/&gt;
            child = getChildElementWithName(nodes&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;i&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;, element);&lt;br/&gt;
            if (child == null) &lt;/p&gt;
{
                child = document.createElement(nodes[i]);
                element.appendChild(child);
            }
&lt;p&gt;            element = child;&lt;br/&gt;
        }&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;        if (attName == null) &lt;/p&gt;
{
            CharacterData data = document.createTextNode(value.toString());
            child.appendChild(data);
        }
&lt;p&gt; else &lt;/p&gt;
{
            child.setAttribute(attName, value.toString());
        }</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12341692">CONFIGURATION-34</key>
            <summary>[configuration] XMLConfiguration.addProperty doesn&apos;t create new child nodes</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="2" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/critical.svg">Critical</priority>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-33] [configuration] Clarify ReloadingStrategy interface usage</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-33</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;I had some trouble creating a ReloadingStrategy implementation (based on a JMX&lt;br/&gt;
reload request) : &lt;br/&gt;
reloadingRequired() is called several times AFTER first returning &apos;true&apos; and&lt;br/&gt;
before reloadingPerformed() is called. In fact, reloading process requires&lt;br/&gt;
access to getProperty() that itself (re)enters reload. If reloadingRequired()&lt;br/&gt;
doens&apos;t return false at this time, a infinite recursice loop starts.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Perhaps it is a reload() bug, that may use a boolean flag to mark&lt;br/&gt;
processing-reload and avoid such infinite loop in the Thread runing he reload.&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>
        <key id="12342555">CONFIGURATION-33</key>
            <summary>[configuration] Clarify ReloadingStrategy interface usage</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="ndeloof">nicolas de loof</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Thu, 15 Sep 2005 17:31:05 +0000</created>
                <updated>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:39 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:39 +0000</resolved>
                                    <version>1.1</version>
                                    <fixVersion>1.2</fixVersion>
                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12410404" author="ebourg" created="Thu, 15 Sep 2005 17:57:30 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Why does the reloading process require access to the properties ?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410405" author="ndeloof" created="Thu, 15 Sep 2005 18:07:56 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;On every line read (I&apos;m using PropertiesConfiguration), addPropertyDirect() is&lt;br/&gt;
called.&lt;br/&gt;
In BaseConfiguration, addPropertyDirect() uses getProperty() to get previous&lt;br/&gt;
property value. If previous value exists or is a List instance, new object is&lt;br/&gt;
added to it (into the existing or into a new list).&lt;br/&gt;
In other cases, new value is simple added to store.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;So getProperty() is called, and enter a second time info reload(). If at this&lt;br/&gt;
time reloadingStrategy doesn&apos;t return false, an infinite loop starts.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410406" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Tue, 20 Sep 2005 00:59:51 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;AbstractFileConfiguration has the two methods enterNoReload() and exitNoReload()&lt;br/&gt;
that manage a flag, which avoids recursive invocation of the reload() method. So&lt;br/&gt;
far these methods are manually called by some sub classes of&lt;br/&gt;
AbstractFileConfiguration, e.g. PropertiesConfiguration.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It will probably make sense to call these methods in reload(), too. This should&lt;br/&gt;
solve this problem.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12410407" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Mon, 7 Nov 2005 04:01:19 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I added calls to enterNoReload() and exitNoReload() to&lt;br/&gt;
AbstractFileConfiguration&apos;s reload() method. This should avoid infinite loops,&lt;br/&gt;
the reloading strategy will be asked only once whether reloading is required.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                    </comments>

            <title>[CONFIGURATION-32] [configuration] XMLConfiguration.save() doesn&apos;t escape reserved characters</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-32</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;If an XML configuration contains a property with a &apos;&amp;lt;&apos; character or an attribute&lt;br/&gt;
property with a quote &apos;&quot;&apos;, the value is not properly escaped with &amp;lt; or &amp;quot;&lt;br/&gt;
in the saved configuration, resulting in an error the next time the&lt;br/&gt;
configuration is loaded.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;For example:&lt;br/&gt;
conf.setProperty(&quot;foo&quot;, &quot;1&amp;lt;2&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
conf.setProperty(&quot;foo&lt;span class=&quot;error&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;@bar&amp;#93;&lt;/span&gt;&quot;, &quot;1\&quot;2&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
conf.save();&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;will generate the following file:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;foo bar=&quot;1&quot;2&quot;&amp;gt;1&amp;lt;2&amp;lt;/foo&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-30] [configuration] MapConfiguration does not decode escaped Delimiters</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-30</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;If a Map handed to MapConfiguration which contains entries with escaped&lt;br/&gt;
delimiters in the value, i.e. &quot;\,&quot;, it is not decoded.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;-&lt;del&gt;code-sample&lt;/del&gt;-&lt;br/&gt;
Map m = new HashMap();&lt;br/&gt;
m.put(&quot;foo&quot;, &quot;bar&lt;br class=&quot;atl-forced-newline&quot; /&gt;, baz&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
m.put(&quot;bar&quot;, &quot;bar, baz&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
Configuration c = new MapConfiguration(m);&lt;br/&gt;
String bad = c.getString(&quot;foo&quot;); &amp;lt;-- returns &quot;bar&lt;br class=&quot;atl-forced-newline&quot; /&gt;, baz&quot; expected &quot;bar, baz&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
String ok = c.getString(&quot;bar&quot;); // &amp;lt;-- returns &quot;bar&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
-&lt;del&gt;code-sample&lt;/del&gt;-&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;It seems that MapConfiguration should employ a similar strategy like&lt;br/&gt;
PropertiesConfiguration - calling undecodeJava on the return value...&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

                            <comment id="12478024" author="polakm" created="Mon, 5 Mar 2007 12:55:49 +0000"  grouplevel="jira-users" >&lt;p&gt;Hello,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;I would like to reopen this bug because I think it still exists.&lt;br/&gt;
There is BAD implementation in MapConfiguration.getProperty(String key) method:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;As &quot;return value&quot; should be list.get(0) instead of &quot;value&quot;.&lt;br/&gt;
PropertyConverter.split removes escape chars....&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Suggested correction:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;    public Object getProperty(String key)&lt;br/&gt;
    {&lt;br/&gt;
        Object value = map.get(key);&lt;br/&gt;
        if ((value instanceof String) &amp;amp;&amp;amp; (!isDelimiterParsingDisabled()))&lt;/p&gt;
        {
            List list = PropertyConverter.split((String) value, getListDelimiter());
            //MP: return list.size() &amp;gt; 1 ? list : value;
            return list.size() &amp;gt; 1 ? list : list.get(0); //MP: split removes escape chars
        }
&lt;p&gt;        else&lt;/p&gt;
        {
            return value;
        }
&lt;p&gt;    }&lt;/p&gt;


&lt;p&gt;Test code:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Map m = new HashMap();&lt;br/&gt;
m.put(&quot;foo&quot;, &quot;bar&lt;br class=&quot;atl-forced-newline&quot; /&gt;,baz&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
m.put(&quot;bar&quot;, &quot;bar, baz&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
MapConfiguration mc = new MapConfiguration(m);&lt;br/&gt;
mc.setDelimiterParsingDisabled(false);&lt;br/&gt;
mc.setListDelimiter(&apos;,&apos;);&lt;br/&gt;
Configuration c = mc;&lt;br/&gt;
String bad = c.getString(&quot;foo&quot;); //&amp;lt;-- returns &quot;bar&lt;br class=&quot;atl-forced-newline&quot; /&gt;, baz&quot; expected &quot;bar, baz&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
String ok = c.getString(&quot;bar&quot;); // &amp;lt;-- returns &quot;bar&quot;&lt;br/&gt;
System.err.println(&quot;Bad: &quot; + bad);&lt;br/&gt;
System.err.println(&quot;OK: &quot; + ok);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Current result is:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Bad: bar\,baz&lt;br/&gt;
OK: bar&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-29] [configuration] SubsetConfiguration.getKeys() always appends &quot;.&quot; delimiter to prefix</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-29</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;When creating a SubsetConfiguration object, e.g.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;conf = new SubsetConfiguration(parentConf, &quot;myprefixwithadot.&quot;);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;calls to conf.getProperty(&quot;prop&quot;) result in a call to&lt;br/&gt;
parent.conf(conf.getPrefix() + &quot;prop&quot;) as expected.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;However, a key iterator obtained by calling conf.getKeys() will only iterate&lt;br/&gt;
over keys starting with (conf.getPrefix() + &quot;.&quot;). In the example, this will be&lt;br/&gt;
&quot;myprefixwithadot..&quot;. There should not be a dot appended. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The error is probably caused by line #283 in AbstractConfiguration.java&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;return key.startsWith(prefix + &quot;.&quot;) || key.equals(prefix);&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: All&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: All&lt;/p&gt;</environment>
        <key id="12342072">CONFIGURATION-29</key>
            <summary>[configuration] SubsetConfiguration.getKeys() always appends &quot;.&quot; delimiter to prefix</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="3" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/major.svg">Major</priority>
                        <status id="5" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/resolved.png" description="A resolution has been taken, and it is awaiting verification by reporter. From here issues are either reopened, or are closed.">Resolved</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="1">Fixed</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="timothomas@web.de">Timo Thomas</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Wed, 23 Feb 2005 00:14:53 +0000</created>
                <updated>Tue, 16 May 2006 11:23:49 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Tue, 16 May 2006 11:23:49 +0000</resolved>
                                                                        <due></due>

                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12408768" author="joerg.schaible@gmx.de" created="Wed, 23 Feb 2005 00:19:07 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;This is how it is supposed to work. Creating a subset always means a subset of a&lt;br/&gt;
(valid) tree.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12408769" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Wed, 23 Feb 2005 00:40:04 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Timo,&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;what you have spotted may be a little inconsistency in the collaboration of&lt;br/&gt;
SubsetConfiguration and its parent configuration, but I don&apos;t think it is critical.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Why do you create your subset configuration by hand? You should rather use the&lt;br/&gt;
subset() method of the Configuration interface for this purpose. This method&lt;br/&gt;
correctly sets the delimiter. The key you pass into subset() should not end with&lt;br/&gt;
a dot. Then everything should work as expected.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12408770" author="ebourg" created="Wed, 23 Feb 2005 00:40:21 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;On the other hand we might remove any trailing dot in the prefix. &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Why do you need a prefix ending with a dot ? Couldn&apos;t you simply use&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;conf = new SubsetConfiguration(parentConf, &quot;prefix&quot;);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;instead of&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;conf = new SubsetConfiguration(parentConf, &quot;prefix.&quot;);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;?&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12408771" author="timothomas@web.de" created="Wed, 23 Feb 2005 01:26:02 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;You are right. I can use subset(&quot;prefix&quot;) and it automatically appends a dot.&lt;br/&gt;
Creating a subset that way getKeys() works as expected. I didn&apos;t see the&lt;br/&gt;
subset() method at first and was misguided by the constructor&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;SubsetConfiguration(Configuration parent, java.lang.String prefix,&lt;br/&gt;
java.lang.String delimiter)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;which made me believe there is no default delimiter.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Thanks for the fast reply.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12408772" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Sun, 6 Mar 2005 02:49:14 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;I updated the documentation to point out that SubsetConfiguration should not be&lt;br/&gt;
used directly and referred to the subset() method of Configuration. This is&lt;br/&gt;
hopefully enough to avoid wrong usage of this class.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                    </comments>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-28] [configuration] Interpolation method returns multi-valued properties</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-28</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;If the property referred to from a variable contains multiple values, the&lt;br/&gt;
interpolation method returns all of these values. This leads to a string&lt;br/&gt;
representation of the list with the properties, which in most cases won&apos;t be&lt;br/&gt;
desired.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Because the interpolation method is called only by getString() and for&lt;br/&gt;
interpolating single elements of a String[] only a single value should be&lt;br/&gt;
returned, i.e. in case of a multi-valued property the first value (which is&lt;br/&gt;
consistent with the behavior of other scalar getter methods).&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment>&lt;p&gt;Operating System: other&lt;br/&gt;
Platform: Other&lt;/p&gt;</environment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-27] [configuration] subset method on xml configuration does not work as expected</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-27</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description></description>
                <environment></environment>
        <key id="12342312">CONFIGURATION-27</key>
            <summary>[configuration] subset method on xml configuration does not work as expected</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/blocker.svg">Blocker</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
                                    <resolution id="4">Incomplete</resolution>
                                        <assignee username="-1">Unassigned</assignee>
                                    <reporter username="fabien.nisol@videotron.ca">Fabien Nisol</reporter>
                        <labels>
                    </labels>
                <created>Thu, 16 Jun 2005 01:50:52 +0000</created>
                <updated>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:39 +0000</updated>
                            <resolved>Sat, 22 Aug 2009 19:36:39 +0000</resolved>
                                    <version>1.1</version>
                                    <fixVersion>1.2</fixVersion>
                                        <due></due>
                            <votes>0</votes>
                                    <watches>0</watches>
                                                                <comments>
                            <comment id="12409621" author="fabien.nisol@videotron.ca" created="Thu, 16 Jun 2005 01:55:30 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;in following example:&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;configuration&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;test1&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;test&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
       &amp;lt;param&amp;gt;value1&amp;lt;/param&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;/test&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;test&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
       &amp;lt;param&amp;gt;value2&amp;lt;/param&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
    &amp;lt;/test&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
  &amp;lt;/test1&amp;gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&amp;lt;/configuration&amp;gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;doing subset like this:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Configuration subcfg = xmlCfg.subset(&quot;test1(1)&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
ConfigurationUtils.dump(subcfg,System.err);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;should output:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;test.param=value2&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;but output:&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;test.param=null&lt;/p&gt;
</comment>
                            <comment id="12409622" author="fabien.nisol@videotron.ca" created="Thu, 16 Jun 2005 01:57:05 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;in example, &lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Configuration subcfg = xmlCfg.subset(&quot;test1(1)&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
ConfigurationUtils.dump(subcfg,System.err);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;should be read&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Configuration subcfg = xmlCfg.subset(&quot;test1.test(1)&quot;);&lt;br/&gt;
ConfigurationUtils.dump(subcfg,System.err);&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Anyway, i&apos;m writing example code that I&apos;m planning to attach to this bug in a&lt;br/&gt;
few minutes.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409623" author="fabien.nisol@videotron.ca" created="Thu, 16 Jun 2005 02:34:11 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;sorry, After investigation, the real source of the problem is when a tag is&lt;br/&gt;
using dots (&amp;lt;a.variable&amp;gt;)&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Apparently, XMLConfiguration does not support this.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Should it ? &lt;/p&gt;</comment>
                            <comment id="12409624" author="oliver.heger@t-online.de" created="Fri, 17 Jun 2005 17:19:54 +0000"  >&lt;p&gt;Yes, I think it should. But I am not sure what&apos;s the best way of implementing&lt;br/&gt;
this. Perhaps by allowing to escape the dot in a tag somehow. Will have to think&lt;br/&gt;
about it.&lt;/p&gt;</comment>

<item>
            <title>[CONFIGURATION-26] Consider returning a concatenation of the list properties with getString()</title>
                <link>https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/CONFIGURATION-26</link>
                <project id="12310467" key="CONFIGURATION">Commons Configuration</project>
                    <description>&lt;p&gt;in AbstractConfiguration.resolveContainerStore (javadoc):&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;ul&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;Returns an object from the store described by the key. If the value is a&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;li&gt;List object, replace it with the first object in the list.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;


&lt;p&gt;but what if getProperty returns a List because this is the type of the property? &lt;br/&gt;
 this code will silently grab the first elemen. I don&apos;t understand why. Probably &lt;br/&gt;
the reason is that some class extending AbstractConfiguration returns List for &lt;br/&gt;
properties. In this case I think the better approach is to have that class &lt;br/&gt;
return the first element instead, rather than returning the List and letting &lt;br/&gt;
AbstractConfiguration (which is used by many other implementations, including &lt;br/&gt;
outside of the configuration package) handle it&lt;/p&gt;</description>
                <environment></environment>
        <key id="12342125">CONFIGURATION-26</key>
            <summary>Consider returning a concatenation of the list properties with getString()</summary>
                <type id="1" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/secure/viewavatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=21133&amp;avatarType=issuetype">Bug</type>
                                            <priority id="4" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/priorities/minor.svg">Minor</priority>
                        <status id="6" iconUrl="https://issues.apache.org/jira/images/icons/statuses/closed.png" description="The issue is considered finished, the resolution is correct. Issues which are not closed can be reopened.">Closed</status>
                    <statusCategory id="3" key="done" colorName="green"/>
